**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is June, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:
Breaking political news

Legislation and policy discussions
Elections, political figures, and government actions

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

**Step 1 (logic-heavy)**

Define the Categories: 

Read through the titles of hundreds of news articles and think carefully.  Use your memory fully. Define major areas, and define specific topics under each area, in a hierarchical way. Every news article should have its best-fitting category. There should be two hierarchical tiers (area, topic), instead of three, and then we get down to individual articles. You should consider this very carefully, making the categories the most helpful for human cognition. Control the total number of areas to 5-8, depending on how diverse and complex the topics are. ### **Explanation of Revisions:**

1.  **Reorganization of the Main Story (Iran-Israel Conflict):** The original draft separated the conflict, the congressional response, and the market reaction into different areas. The revised structure consolidates all facets of the Iran-Israel conflict under **Area 1: Foreign Policy & National Security**. This provides a more holistic view, with distinct topics for the on-the-ground military/ceasefire developments (1.1), the political fallout and commentary (1.2), and the direct economic consequences like oil prices (1.3).

2.  **Consolidation into Five Areas:** The initial six areas have been streamlined into five. The original "Economic & Financial Developments" area was dissolved because its primary articles (oil prices, stock futures) were directly tied to the Iran conflict and have been moved to Topic 1.3 for better context.

3.  **Creation of a "Presidential Affairs" Topic:** A new topic, **Topic 2.4: Presidential Affairs, Administration, & Oversight**, was created under the Executive Branch area. This provides a more logical home for articles concerning the President's business dealings (Trump Organization loan), his staff (Press Secretary profile), and general administrative actions (VA contract cuts, federal data collection), which previously were in a miscellaneous "General Governance" or "Corporate Finance" category.

4.  **Refined Topic Naming for Clarity:** Topic names have been edited for brevity and precision. For instance, "Executive Branch: Domestic Policy & Regulatory Actions" was shortened to "Executive Branch: Domestic Policy & Governance." "Immigration Enforcement and Agency Conduct" is now simply "Immigration & Border Enforcement." This enhances readability and makes the hierarchy more intuitive.

5.  **Reordering of Areas:** The Areas have been reordered to present a more logical flow for a Congressional audience: International affairs first, then the actions of the Executive Branch, followed by Congress's own activities, the Judiciary's rulings affecting them all, and finally State & Local issues.

However, the deal's viability was immediately undermined when Iran’s foreign minister stated no "final decision" had been reached, and Iranian air defenses reportedly remained active [2]. **DAILY BRIEFING FOR CONGRESSIONAL LEADERSHIP**

**DATE:** June 14, 2025

**FROM:** Office of the Chief News Analyst

**SUBJECT:** Unraveling Iran Ceasefire; SCOTUS Backs Administration on Immigration; GOP "Megabill" Hits Roadblocks

**TOPLINE ASSESSMENT:** The security and diplomatic landscape is in crisis as a U.S.-brokered ceasefire between Israel and Iran has all but collapsed, prompting volatile market reactions and sharp domestic debate over presidential war powers. ### **Area 1: Foreign Policy & National Security**

**Topic 1.1: Iran-Israel Ceasefire Collapses Amid Renewed Hostilities**

A ceasefire announced by President Trump to end a "12 Day War" between Israel and Iran is in a state of disintegration [1]. The deal's viability was immediately undermined when Iran’s foreign minister stated no "final decision" had been reached [2]. The situation deteriorated rapidly after Israel accused Iran of a new missile strike and ordered military retaliation, leading to reports that the ceasefire had completely unraveled [3]. This collapse prompted a public display of frustration from President Trump, who, in response to the continued fighting, was quoted as saying, "They don’t know what the f--- they’re doing" [4]. The swift breakdown from a declared diplomatic achievement to open conflict signifies a severe escalation in the region.

**Topic 1.2: Escalating Domestic Debate Over Presidential War Powers**

The strikes on Iran have ignited a fierce domestic debate over the legality of the President's actions and have fractured political consensus. A report alleges Prime Minister Netanyahu decided on war with Iran last year and then worked to "recruit Trump" to the cause, raising questions about the conflict's origins [1]. The President's use of military force has prompted legal analyses of presidential war powers and led House Democrats to introduce legislation aimed at limiting his authority [2, 3]. The response has crossed party lines, with some Republicans clashing with the administration over the strikes, and Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene highlighting a divide within the MAGA movement by stating supporters wanted "no more foreign wars" [4, 5]. Amid this, experts warn of Iran's significant cyberattack capabilities and doubt whether the military action has meaningfully crippled its nuclear ambitions, potentially dragging the U.S. into a "quagmire" [6, 7].

**Topic 1.3: Markets React to Middle East Volatility**

Financial markets are displaying significant volatility in response to the fast-moving events in the Middle East. U.S. stock futures saw an initial surge following President Trump's ceasefire announcement, reflecting market optimism for de-escalation [1]. Energy markets have been particularly unstable. Oil prices first dropped sharply on reports that the initial U.S. strikes had deliberately avoided Iranian crude infrastructure, but then trimmed those losses as subsequent Iranian missile tests challenged the fragile truce [2, 3]. As the ceasefire continued to wobble, oil prices extended their losses, indicating broad market uncertainty over the conflict's duration and potential economic impact [4].

### **Area 2: Judiciary & Legal System**

**Topic 2.1: Supreme Court Sides With Administration on Immigration Policy**

The Supreme Court delivered a major victory to the administration on immigration, ruling to allow the resumption of "3rd-country removals" of migrants without previous "court-ordered due process requirements" [1]. Critics argue the decision effectively strips due process rights from thousands of immigrants [2]. The ruling drew an exceptionally sharp dissent from the Court's liberal justices. In a scathing rebuke, Justice Sotomayor accused the conservative majority of "rewarding lawlessness" by the Trump administration [3].

### **Area 3: Executive Branch: Domestic Policy & Governance**

**Topic 3.1: HHS Secretary Kennedy Drives Major Health Policy Changes**

HHS Secretary Robert F. Kennedy, Jr. is actively reshaping federal health policy. Reports indicate he is "Taking an Axe to America’s Dietary Guidelines," signaling a fundamental shift in nutritional advice [1]. In a joint initiative with CMS Administrator Oz, Secretary Kennedy has also secured an industry "pledge" from insurers to reform the "broken prior authorization system" [2]. These actions coincide with the administration replacing members on a key federal vaccine advisory panel. This move is reportedly causing outside health groups to seek ways to "preserve vaccine access, bypassing RFK Jr." and his perceived influence on immunization policy [3].

Simultaneously, a proposal for "massive NOAA cuts" has sparked warnings from experts that such a move would imperil the accuracy of weather forecasting and endanger lives [2]. **Topic 4.1: GOP "Megabill" Stalls on Procedural Hurdles**

The Republican majority’s primary legislative vehicle, a "megabill" intended to pass via budget reconciliation, is facing critical procedural roadblocks from the Senate Parliamentarian. The parliamentarian has ruled against key conservative priorities, finding that a proposed "civil service overhaul" and provisions to expand offshore oil and gas drilling violate the Byrd Rule and therefore cannot be included in the bill [1, 2]. A separate ruling also blocked an effort to force the U.S. Postal Service to scrap its electric vehicle fleet [3]. These procedural defeats weaken the package and exacerbate political tensions within the GOP. One Republican senator has already warned that proposed Medicaid cuts could "derail" the entire legislative effort, highlighting the fragile nature of the majority coalition [4].

**FROM:** Office of the Chief News Analyst

**SUBJECT:** Unraveling Iran Ceasefire; SCOTUS Backs Administration on Immigration; GOP "Megabill" Hits Roadblocks

**TOPLINE ASSESSMENT:** The security and diplomatic landscape is in crisis as a U.S.-brokered ceasefire between Israel and Iran has all but collapsed, prompting volatile market reactions and sharp domestic debate over presidential war powers. In Washington, a landmark Supreme Court ruling has sided with the administration on immigration removals, inviting a scathing dissent from the Court’s liberal wing and amplifying tensions over executive authority. Concurrently, the majority’s signature legislative effort, a "megabill" leveraging budget reconciliation, faces critical setbacks from the Senate Parliamentarian, jeopardizing key policy goals and exposing intra-party fractures. Meanwhile, significant policy shifts in health and environment, coupled with controversial actions at the state level and by federal agencies like ICE, are creating a complex and volatile domestic political environment. These events represent the most immediate crises requiring leadership’s attention.

A ceasefire announced by President Trump to end a "12 Day War" between Israel and Iran is in a state of disintegration [1]. The deal's viability was immediately undermined when Iran’s foreign minister stated no "final decision" had been reached [2]. The situation deteriorated rapidly after Israel accused Iran of a new missile strike and ordered military retaliation, leading to reports that the ceasefire had completely unraveled [3]. This collapse prompted a public display of frustration from President Trump, who, in response to the continued fighting, was quoted as saying, "They don’t know what the f--- they’re doing" [4]. The swift breakdown from a declared diplomatic achievement to open conflict signifies a severe escalation in the region.

The parliamentarian has ruled against key conservative priorities, finding that a proposed "civil service overhaul" and provisions to expand offshore oil and gas drilling violate the Byrd Rule and therefore cannot be included in the bill [1, 2]. These procedural defeats weaken the package and exacerbate political tensions within the GOP. One Republican senator has already warned that proposed Medicaid cuts could "derail" the entire legislative effort, highlighting the fragile nature of the majority coalition [4].

**References:**
[1] GOP civil service overhaul effort violates reconciliation rules, https://federalnewsnetwork.com/congress/2025/06/gop-civil-service-overhaul-effort-violates-reconciliation-rules/  
[2] Senate parliamentarian rejects offshore oil, gas drilling provisions in GOP megabill, https://thehill.com/homenews/senate/5365699-senate-parliamentarian-offshore-drilling-gop-megabill/  
[3] Senate Republicans cannot force US Postal Service to scrap EVs, parliamentarian says, https://www.reuters.com/business/autos-transportation/senate-republicans-cannot-force-us-postal-service-scrap-evs-parliamentarian-says-2025-06-23/  
[4] GOP senator warns Medicaid cuts could derail Trump megabill, https://thehill.com/homenews/senate/5365429-josh-hawley-medicaid-cuts-trump-megabill/amp/  

### 4.2 Murkowski Move and Partisan Activities Signal Political Volatility

A potentially pivotal development is emerging in the Senate, where Senator Lisa Murkowski (R-AK) has "left the door open" to the possibility of caucusing with the Democrats [1]. Given the narrow 53-47 Republican majority, any such realignment would have profound consequences for the balance of power. While this unfolds, other political activities continue. Senator Bernie Sanders (I-VT) held a large, "fiery" anti-Trump rally in Fort Worth, Texas, declaring the state central to the "future of American politics" [2]. On a more ceremonial note, Republicans defeated Democrats in the annual Congressional Baseball Game for the fifth consecutive year [3].

**References:**
[1] Murkowski leaves door open to scenario of caucusing with Democrats, https://www.axios.com/2025/06/24/murkowski-book-democrats-alaska-senate  
[2] At fiery Fort Worth rally, Bernie Sanders galvanizes crowd with anti-Trump message | “The future of American politics rests in Texas,” the senator from Vermont said., https://www.dallasnews.com/news/politics/2025/06/22/at-fiery-fort-worth-rally-bernie-sanders-galvanizes-crowd-with-anti-trump-message/

## 5. State and Local Governance

### 5.1 States Pursue Divergent Policies on Major Issues

Key states are taking bold actions that conflict with federal precedent and, in some cases, their own party's consensus. In a significant energy development, New York is planning to construct one of the nation's first new nuclear power plants in a generation [1]. In Texas, officials are moving forward with a plan to place the Ten Commandments in all public schools, a policy described as being "in defiance of courts" [2]. The Texas GOP is also experiencing internal conflict, with Lt. Gov. Dan Patrick publicly criticizing Gov. Greg Abbott's veto of a bill banning THC, accusing the governor of wanting to "legalize recreational marijuana" [3]. In Missouri, state officials have reportedly seized control of the St. Louis police department in what is being framed as a strategic effort to reverse local policing reforms [4].

### 5.2 NYC Mayoral Race Signals Potential National Political Shift

The New York City mayoral race is reportedly nearing its conclusion and is being watched as a bellwether for national political trends. A potential victory for a candidate named Mamdani over a candidate named Cuomo is being framed by observers as a potential "seismic shift in national politics" and a significant test for the socialist movement on a major stage [1].
